Main category: gr-qc

TL;DR: Error


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Error

Method: Error

Result: Error

Conclusion: Error

Abstract: We investigate light propagation in self-gravitating systems composed of an
axially symmetric, stationary, rotating dust fluid. These configurations are
intrinsically relativistic, sustained entirely by their rotation, since no
compact or finite dust distribution can exist under the same symmetry
conditions in Newtonian gravity. In such systems, rotational effects arise from
off-diagonal components of the spacetime metric, which are not negligible
compared to their Newtonian counterparts. We analyze how these components
affect the deflection angle of light, showing that they can be interpreted as
contributing an additional effective mass. Moreover, their presence can, in
principle, be detected through the characteristic asymmetry they induce in the
images of background sources.

Abstract: We use the data of several promising gravitational wave observations to
obtain increasingly stringent bounds on near-horizon deviations of their
sources from the Kerr geometry. A range of horizonless compact objects proposed
as alternatives to black holes of general relativity would possess a modified
gravitational wave emission after the merger. Modelling these objects by
introducing reflection of gravitational waves near the horizon, we can measure
deviations from Kerr in terms of a single additional parameter, the location of
the reflection. We quote bounds on deviations for 5 events in addition to
previous results obtained for GW150914. Additionally, we improve upon previous
results by hierarchically combining information from all analysed events,

### [159] [Approximate Ricci-flat Metrics for Calabi-Yau Manifolds](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.15766)
*Seung-Joo Lee,Andre Lukas*

Main category: hep-th

TL;DR: We describe a machine learning method to compute Ricci-flat K"ahler potentials on Calabi-Yau manifolds using Donaldson's Ansatz. The method is applied to two one-parameter families of C-Y manifolds, resulting in analytic expressions dependent on the modulus of the complex structure parameter. Our results demonstrate the effectiveness of machine learning in approximating Ricci-flat metrics and provide explicit expressions for these potentials, which could be useful in string compactifications and geometric modeling in high-energy physics.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: The paper presents an innovative approach to computing Ricci-flat K"ahler metrics on Calabi-Yau manifolds, which are important in string theory and algebraic geometry. The use of machine learning to approximate these metrics is exciting, as analytically solving for Ricci-flat metrics is notoriously difficult. This method provides a new tool for researchers in these fields to study the geometry of Calabi-Yau manifolds and their applications in physics.

Method: The authors employ machine learning as a numerical approach to solve for the Ricci-flat K"ahler potentials. They use Donaldson's Ansatz, which suggests a specific form for the potential, to fit their numerical results. By extracting features from high-dimensional datasets generated by numerical methods, they train a model to approximate the potential functions. The key steps involve numerical computation of Ricci-flat metrics, applying Donaldson's Ansatz, and using the trained model to derive analytic expressions.

Result: The researchers successfully applied their machine learning-based method to two distinct one-parameter families of Calabi-Yau manifolds. They obtained analytic expressions for the Ricci-flat K"ahler potentials, which depend solely on the modulus of the complex structure parameter. These explicit forms are a significant simplification compared to previous numerical results and could lead to applications in theoretical physics.

Conclusion: This work opens up new possibilities for using machine learning in geometric analysis, particularly in constructing Ricci-flat metrics. The explicit analytic expressions derived not only validate the approach but also provide concrete tools for further research into the geometry of Calabi-Yau manifolds and their roles in string theory.

Abstract: We outline a method to determine analytic K\"ahler potentials with associated
approximately Ricci-flat K\"ahler metrics on Calabi-Yau manifolds. Key
ingredients are numerically calculating Ricci-flat K\"ahler potentials via
machine learning techniques and fitting the numerical results to Donaldson's
Ansatz. We apply this method to the Dwork family of quintic hypersurfaces in
$\mathbb{P}^4$ and an analogous one-parameter family of bi-cubic CY
hypersurfaces in $\mathbb{P}^2\times\mathbb{P}^2$. In each case, a relatively
simple analytic expression is obtained for the approximately Ricci-flat
K\"ahler potentials, including the explicit dependence on the complex structure
parameter. We find that these K\"ahler potentials only depend on the modulus of
the complex structure parameter.

### [160] [The Hidden Symmetries of Yang-Mills Theory in (3+1)-dimensions](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.15832)
*L. A. Ferreira,H. Malavazzi*

Main category: hep-th

TL;DR: 该论文研究了经典非超对称杨-米尔斯理论与自旋1/2和自旋0基本物质场在(3+1)维Minkowski时空中的可积性结构，发现其具有无限多个正则相互作用的保守电荷，并基于非阿贝尔电荷和磁荷的广义环路空间，提出R矩阵和Sklyanin关系。研究了两个新的杨-米尔斯理论对称性。第一个是通过无限个保守电荷生成的整体变换，涉及场和Wilson线 flux的变换规律。第二个是积分杨-米尔斯方程的对称性，生成无限维群，其中元是时空上的环路空间函数。这些结果适用于标准模型，保守电荷是规范不变的，且在QCD中构成色零态，可能未被束缚。因此， Hadrons可能携带这些电荷。该成果为杨-米尔斯非扰理论方法铺平了道路。


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: 研究经典非超对称杨-米尔斯理论的可积性结构，有助于理解其对称性及其在粒子物理中的应用，尤其是强相互作用力的理论方法。

Method: 论文通过探讨杨-米尔斯理论中电荷的构造，引入广义环路空间、R矩阵和Sklyanin关系，揭示了理论的可积结构。发现了两个新的对称性，分别涉及整体变换和积分方程的对称性，并应用于标准模型，探讨了这类电荷在QCD中的表现。

Result: 杨-米尔斯理论在经典非超对称情况下，在(3+1)维时空具有可积性结构，即无限多的正则相互作用的保守电荷。这些电荷基于广义的环路空间，引入了R矩阵和Sklyanin关系。发现了两个对称性：整体变换由无限多个保守电荷生成，积分方程的对称性生成无限维群。这些结果适用于标准模型，支持QCD中的色零态可能存在未被束缚的行为， Hadrons可能携带这些电荷，为非扰理论方法铺平了道路。

Conclusion: 该理论在经典非超对称情况下具有可积性结构，适用于标准模型，揭示了新的对称性和保守电荷，并为研究色电荷和强相互作用提供了新的视角和方法。这为探索非扰杨-米尔斯理论提供了理论基础。

Abstract: We show that classical, non-supersymmetric Yang-Mills theories coupled to
spin-1/2 and spin-0 elementary matter fields, in (3+1)-dimensional Minkowski
space-time, possess an exact integrability structure with an infinite number of
conserved charges in involution. Such an integrability lives on the space of
non-abelian electric and magnetic charges, and is based on flat connections in
generalized loop spaces, presenting an R-matrix, and Sklyanin relation. We
present two novel symmetries of Yang-Mills theories. The first one corresponds
to global transformations generated by the infinity of those conserved charges
under the Poisson brackets. The gauge and matter fields, as well as Wilson
lines and fluxes have interesting transformation laws under such a global
symmetry. The second one corresponds to symmetries of the integral Yang-Mills
equations, which lead to the conserved charges. They generate an infinite
dimensional group, where the elements are holonomies of connections on the loop
space of functions from the circle $S^1$ to the space-time. Our approach
certainly applies to the Standard Model of the Fundamental Interactions. The
conserved charges are gauge invariant, and so, in the case of QCD they are
color singlets, and perhaps are not confined. Therefore, the hadrons may carry
such charges. Our results open up the way for the construction of
non-perturbative methods for Yang-Mills theories.

</details>


### [161] [How to Count States in Gravity](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.15767)
*Vijay Balasubramanian,Tom Yildirim*

Main category: hep-th

TL;DR: 该摘要表明，Gibbons和Hawking提出的路径积分方法可以用来计算引力系统的熵，并解释了为何这种方法有效。


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: 研究量子引力中的熵计算方法，尤其是Gibbons和Hawking的方法，有助于理解引力系统的热力学性质和熵的计算机制。

Method: 摘要中展示了通过路径积分计算热体的迹，进而解释了熵的计算。作者通过分解路径积分和计算迹的方式，证明了这一方法的有效性。

Result: 研究证实了路径积分与热力学迹之间的等价性，说明了Gibbons和Hawking方法的正确性，为计算引力熵提供了理论依据。

Conclusion: 该方法提供了计算引力系统熵的新方法，通过路径积分计算热力学迹，从而解释熵的物理意义。

Abstract: Gibbons and Hawking proposed that the Euclidean gravity path integral with
periodic boundary conditions in time computes the thermal partition sum of
gravity. As a corollary, they argued that a derivative of the associated free
energy with respect to the Euclidean time period computes gravitational
entropy. Why is this interpretation is correct? That is, why does this path
integral compute a trace over the Hilbert space? Here, we show that the
quantity computed by the Gibbons-Hawking path integral is equal to an {\it a
priori} different object -- an explicit thermal trace over the Hilbert space
spanned by states produced by the Euclidean gravity path integral. This follows
in two ways: (a) if the Hilbert space with two boundaries factorizes into a
product of two single boundary Hilbert spaces, as we have previously shown; and
(b) via explicit resolution of the trace by a spanning basis of states. We
similarly show how a replicated Euclidean gravity path integral with a single
periodic boundary computes a Hilbert space trace of powers of the density
matrix, explaining why this approach computes the entropy of states entangled
between two universes.

</details>

  <summary>Details</summary>

Method: 该研究通过构造适当的IIB超引力背景，实施超对称环面约化，计算了几何和场论上的各种量，如CS水平、威尔逊环、中心电荷，分析了结果是否与预期的三维Chern-Simons TQFT的性质相符。

Result: 结果显示，当Nf等于2倍的Nc时，超引力背景成立且观察到的三维相是一致的。

Conclusion: 该研究通过超对称紧致化方法，揭示了四维规范理论紧致化与三维Chern-Simons TQFT之间的关系，强调了超对称、异常和几何在规范理论在紧致化中的相互作用。

Abstract: We construct and analyse holographic duals to a class of four-dimensional N =
1 SU($N_c$) SQCD-like theories compactified on a circle with an R-symmetry
twist. The setup originates from type IIB backgrounds previously proposed as
duals to SQCD with $N_f$ fundamental flavours. The U(1) R-symmetry is
anomaly-free only if $ N_f = 2N_c$. We implement a supersymmetric
twisted-circle reduction, holographically realised through a smoothly shrinking
$S^1$ fibered over the internal U(1)$_R$ direction. We obtain new regular type
IIB supergravity backgrounds that are valid only if the condition $N_f = 2N_c$
is satisfied--mirroring the anomaly cancellation requirement in the field
theory. We compute various field-theoretic observables--including the

emergence of a 3D ${\cal N} = 2$ gapped phase consistent with a Chern-Simons
TQFT. This work highlights the interplay between anomalies, supersymmetry, and

modification breaks parity although it does not affect the equations of motion.
We show that the standard Komar charge is also modified by the addition of a
topological term multiplied by the Barbero parameter $\alpha$. For the Killing
vector that generates time translations, the value of the Komar integral at
infinity is modified by the addition of a term proportional to the NUT charge
$N$ and the parity-breaking Barbero parameter. Thus, as in the standard Witten
effect, a non-vanishing NUT charge $N$ induces a non-vanishing mass $\alpha N$.

### [165] [Observer Time from Causality in Perturbative Quantum Gravity](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.16109)

  <summary>Details</summary>

Abstract: It is unclear whether an observable notion of time exists in quantum gravity
even in principle because spacetime itself fluctuates. We propose a form of
observable time in perturbative quantum gravity. First, we define an elapsed
proper time in curved space using intersections of worldlines and future light
cones. Here, time arises from causality via the dependence on light cones. We
then propose that performing the gravitational path integral describes quantum
gravity corrections to this notion of proper time at all orders in $G_N$. Using
this prescription, we compute the leading quantum gravity corrections to
two-point correlation functions of elapsed time. We find that the commutators
can be nonzero, showing this notion of time is a quantum operator in quantum

Abstract: The Carroll group arises in the vanishing speed of light limit of the
Poincar\'{e} group and was initially discarded as just a mathematical
curiosity. However, recent developments have proved otherwise. Carroll and
conformal Carroll symmetries are now ubiquitous, appearing in diverse physical
phenomena starting from condensed matter physics to quantum gravity. This
review aims to provide the reader a gateway into this fast-developing field.
After an introduction and setting the stage with basics of the symmetry in
question, we detail the construction of Carrollian and Carrollian Conformal
field theories (CCFT).
  We then focus on applications. By far the most popular of these applications
is in the context of the construction of holography in asymptotically flat
spacetimes (AFS) in terms of a co-dimension one dual CCFT. We review the early
work on AFS$_3$ /CCFT$_2$ before delving into an in-depth analysis for the
construction of the dual to 4D AFS.
  Two other important sets of applications are in hydrodynamics and in
condensed matter physics, which we discuss in detail. Carroll hydrodynamics is
introduced as the $c\to 0$ limit of relativistic hydrodynamics first and then
reconstructed from a symmetry based approach. Relations to ultrarelativistic
flows and connections to the quark-gluon plasma are discussed with concrete
examples of the Bjorken and Gubser flow models. In condensed matter
applications, we cover connections to fractons, flat bands, and phase
separation in Luttinger liquid models. To conclude, we give very brief outlines
of other topics of interest including string theory and black hole horizons.

### [168] [Dislocations and crystallization dynamics of chiral soliton lattices](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.16354)
*Minoru Eto,Kentaro Nishimura,Muneto Nitta*

Main category: hep-th

TL;DR: Error


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Error

Method: Error

Result: Error

Conclusion: Error

Abstract: Dislocations, as topological defects in crystal lattices, are fundamental to
understanding plasticity in materials. Similar periodic structures also arise
in continuum field theories, such as chiral soliton lattices (CSLs), which
appear in condensed matter systems like chiral magnets and in high-energy
contexts such as quantum chromodynamics in strong magnetic field or under rapid
rotation. This work investigates whether dislocations can dynamically form
within such emergent CSLs. The chiral sine-Gordon model, reduced from the
aforementioned examples by certain truncations, is useful to determine the
ground state but it cannot describe time evolution, lacks dynamical formation
or leads to singular dislocations, because its equations of motion do not
contain a topological term. We propose a field-theoretical model including the
topological term coupled to external fields resolving these issues by modifying
the topological term so it affects the dynamics. Using numerical simulations,
we study the real-time formation of CSLs in two and three spatial dimensions.
In 2D, edge dislocations emerge spontaneously, guiding soliton growth and later
annihilating to leave a stable CSL. In 3D, both edge and screw dislocations
form; the latter exhibits helical structure influenced by the external field.
We find stable double helical screw dislocations looking like a double helix
staircase or DNA. We then demonstrate the formation of helical dislocations and
analyze how the external field strength affects CSL density and formation
speed. Our results provide a novel theoretical framework for understanding
dislocations in solitonic structures, connecting high-energy field theory with
materials science phenomena.

### [175] [The (No) Boundary Proposal and excited states in de Sitter holography](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.16943)
*Marcelo Botta-Cantcheff,Facundo Lorenzo Cruz,Pedro J. Martinez*

Main category: hep-th

TL;DR: In the AdS/CFT framework, vacuum and excited states are obtained by varying boundary conditions. A similar method is applied to de Sitter, allowing the description of excited states via additional boundaries. The presence of these states is shown to affect late-time observables, with possible implications for de Sitter holography.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: The paper uses the AdS/CFT correspondence as a method to explore excited states in de Sitter spacetime, which is a significant challenge in theoretical physics given the different nature of these two spacetimes. The holographic principle suggests a deep connection between quantum gravity and boundary theories, so exploring this in de Sitter could have important implications. The paper may advance our understanding of holography in non-AdS backgrounds, which is an active and complex field. Furthermore, the results could be relevant for cosmology, as de Sitter space is related to inflationary scenarios. Understanding excited states in such contexts helps bridge the AdS/CFT correspondence to realistic cosmological models. The paper's method of adding boundaries to describe excited states is innovative and could open new avenues for research in both theoretical physics and holography. Additionally, the implications for late-time observations may lead to testable predictions, which is of great interest in modern cosmology.

Method: The authors extend the no boundary proposal, a concept originally used in the AdS/CFT framework by Hawking and others, to describe excited states in de Sitter spacetime. They introduce additional boundaries in the Euclidean region and apply arbitrary Dirichlet boundary conditions to them. The method involves computing correlation functions to determine the consistency of excited states and their effects on late-time observables. The approach builds on established holographic techniques but adapts them to a different spacetime background, emphasizing the AdS-like boundary conditions and their relation to the bulk geometry. The key steps include adding a boundary, setting boundary conditions, computing correlators, and analyzing their implications for observables.

Result: By introducing an additional boundary and arbitrary Dirichlet conditions, the authors demonstrate that excited states in de Sitter spacetime can be consistently defined. Calculations of n-point correlation functions show that these states lead to modifications in late-time cosmological observables. This finding suggests that the holographic dictionary can be extended to de Sitter, offering new insights into the quantum nature of cosmological spacetimes. The modifications in observables imply that theoretical predictions could differ from those in a purely de Sitter background, potentially aligning with observations in inflationary models. The success of this method supports the idea of a holographic correspondence beyond AdS/CFT and opens questions about the role of boundaries and boundary conditions in other spacetime geometries. The results demonstrate the feasibility of describing excited states in de Sitter using similar techniques to AdS, contributing to the broader understanding of holography in curved spacetimes.

Conclusion: The paper presents a novel approach to describing excited states in de Sitter spacetime by extending the no boundary proposal. By introducing an additional boundary and varying Dirichlet conditions, the authors successfully compute correlation functions that indicate excited states and their effect on late-time observables. This work not only advances the theoretical framework for holographic descriptions in de Sitter but also suggests implications for inflationary cosmology, offering new tools for studying quantum gravity in non-AdS settings.

Abstract: In the AdS/CFT framework, vacuum and excited states are systematically
described by imposing arbitrary Dirichlet boundary conditions at the AdS
boundary. Furthermore, there are explicit relations connecting the quantum
states to their corresponding dual Euclidean AdS geometries, in line with the
Hartle-Hawking (HH) construction. The ground state therefore corresponds to the
dominant saddle point under trivial conditions on the asymptotic boundary,
which is the exact Euclidean AdS geometry. In contrast, the situation in de
Sitter spacetime differs significantly, as there is no natural region analogous
to the AdS boundary. Thus, the Hartle Hawking approach precisely defines the
ground state as a path integral over smooth (Euclidean) geometries ending on a
spatial Cauchy surface, with \textit{no} additional boundary or past
singularity, known as the no boundary proposal.
  In this work, we revisit the no boundary proposal to describe excited states
within the framework of de Sitter Holography. Specifically, we investigate the
possibility of defining a family of excited states by introducing an additional
boundary in the Euclidean region and imposing arbitrary Dirichlet boundary
conditions on it. As a result, we demonstrate that the computation of $n$ point
correlation functions is consistent with the presence of excited states, and
furthermore, show that cosmological late-time observables in these states
undergo non-trivial modifications. This study may have significant implications
for the development of the holographic dictionary for de Sitter spacetimes.

</details>

### [177] [The simplest chaos indicator derived from Lagrangian descriptors](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.16660)
*Javier Jiménez-López,Víctor J. García-Garrido*

Main category: nlin.CD

TL;DR: Error


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Error

Method: Error

Result: Error

Conclusion: Error

Abstract: In this paper we introduce the simplest chaos indicator derivable from
Lagrangian Descriptors (LDs), defined as the difference in LD values between
two neighboring trajectories. This difference LD is remarkably easy to
implement and interpret, offering a direct and intuitive measure of dynamical
behavior. We provide a heuristic argument linking its growth to the regularity
or chaoticity of the underlying initial condition, considering both
arclength-based and $p$-norm formulations of LDs. To evaluate its
effectiveness, we benchmark it against more elaborate LD-based chaos indicators
using two prototypical systems: the H\'enon-Heiles system and the Chirikov
Standard Map. Our results show that, despite its simplicity, the difference LD
matches, and in some cases surpasses, the accuracy of more sophisticated
methods, making it a robust and accessible tool for chaos detection in
dynamical systems.

Abstract: Membrane proteins serve a wide range of vital roles in the functioning of

attributed to dust and ice-driven processes.

### [181] [The Phase-Space Way To Electronic Structure Theory and Subsequently Chemical Dynamics](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.15994)
*Xuezhi Bian,Titouan Duston,Nadine Bradbury,Zhen Tao,Mansi Bhati,Tian Qiu,Xinchun Wu,Yanze Wu,Joseph E. Subotnik*

Main category: physics.chem-ph

TL;DR: Phase-space electronic structure theory introduces a new approach that extends beyond the Born-Oppenheimer approximation by including nuclear momentum, allowing for the direct calculation of electronic momentum and vibrational spectral features. The method is exact for the hydrogen atom and improves upon BO theory in some models, offering new perspectives in spin physics such as broken-symmetry ground states. The theory calls for a shift towards diagonalizing the phase-space Hamiltonian rather than the Born-Oppenheimer one.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: The paper introduces a novel theoretical framework that extends the traditional Born-Oppenheimer approximation, offering new insights into molecular and material dynamics, particularly in spin chemistry.

Method: Phase-space electronic structure theory is developed using phase-space mechanics, which includes nuclear momentum as a variable. The method's validity is demonstrated using the hydrogen atom model and compared to BO theory in specific cases.

Result: The method is shown to be exact for the hydrogen atom and provides improved vibrational energy calculations for certain model problems. It also suggests new possibilities in the study of spin states and phenomena in magnetic chemistry.

Conclusion: The paper advocates moving away from the conventional BO approximation and towards incorporating phase-space Hamiltonian diagonalization to better understand and model electronic dynamics, particularly in the context of spin chemistry and magnetic properties of materials.

Abstract: Phase-space electronic structure theory offers up a new and powerful approach
for tackling problems with coupled nuclear-electronic dynamics in a fashion
that goes beyond Born-Oppenheimer (BO) theory. Whereas BO theory stipulates
that we consider electronic states parameterized by nuclear position $X$ only,
i.e. molecular orbitals are functions of nuclear positions but not nuclear
velocities, phase-space (PS) theory allows for electronic states to be
parameterized by both nuclear position X and nuclear momentum $P$. As a result,
within a phase-space approach, one can directly recover many new features,
including electronic momentum and vibrational circular dichroism spectra.
Moreover, phase-space electronic structure theory is exact for the hydrogen
atom and, for a set of model problems, the method can even improve upon
vibrational energies relative to BO theory. Perhaps most importantly, the
phase-space approach offers up a very new perspective on spin physics,
stipulating that molecules and materials with degenerate or nearly degenerate
ground states (due to spin degeneracy) display broken-symmetry ground states in
their phase-space potential energy surfaces. This last feature opens up very
new possibilities for exploring spin chemistry (including the Einstein-de Haas
effect and chiral induced spin selectivity) within the context of more
established electronic structure theory. At the end of the day, in order to
tackle electronic dynamical phenomena, especially subtle problems in magnetic
chemistry, it will be essential for the electronic structure community to pivot
towards diagonalizing $\hat H_{PS}(X, P)$ rather than $\hat H_{BO}(X)$.

</details>

### [184] [Exact static linear response of excited states from ensemble density functional theory](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.16363)
*Lucien Dupuy,Emmanuel Fromager*

TL;DR: The paper extends the ensemble DFT framework to static linear response theory, enabling precise evaluation of excited-state density-density functions without frequency dependence. <details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: The authors build upon their previous work on ensemble DFT to advance the understanding of excited states and their response properties.

Method: They derived static linear response theory for excited states, connected individual state contributions, and used a zero-weight limit approach.

Result: Exact excited-state corrections to ground-state LDFD involve Hxc derivatives, emphasizing the role of weight derivatives in ensemble DFT.

Conclusion: The work paves the way for enhanced descriptive capabilities of ground-state DFT in excited states by considering electron transitions.

Abstract: Following a recent work [E. Fromager, J. Phys. Chem. A 2025, 129, 4,
1143-1155] on the ensemble density functional theory (DFT) of excited
electronic energy levels, we derive in this paper the ensuing static linear
response theory, thus allowing for an in-principle exact evaluation of
excited-state density-density linear response functions in a completely
frequency-independent setting. Once individual-state components of the inverse
ensemble linear response function have been introduced, a working Dyson-type
equation naturally emerges for each state, individually. By considering the
zero-weight limit of the theory, which infinitesimally deviates from standard
Kohn--Sham DFT, exact excited-state corrections to ground-state linear response
DFT can be identified. They involve the first-order weight derivatives of the
ensemble Hartree-exchange-correlation (Hxc) potential and kernel, thus
confirming the importance in ensemble DFT of both weight and density-functional
derivatives of the ensemble Hxc energy functional.

Abstract: The mechanisms by which light interacts with ice and the impact of
photo-induced reactions are central to our understanding of environmental,
atmospheric and astrophysical processes. However, a microscopic description of
the photoproducts originating from UV absorption and emission processes has
remained elusive. Here we explore the photochemistry of ice using
time-dependent hybrid density functional theory on various models of pristine
and defective ice Ih. Our investigation of the excited state potential energy
surface of the crystal shows that UV absorption can lead to the formation of
hydronium ions, hydroxyl radicals and excess electrons. One of the dominant
mechanisms of decay from the excited to the ground-state involves the
recombination of the electron with the hydroxyl radical yielding
hydronium-hydroxide ion-pairs. We find that the details of this charge
recombination process, sensitively depends on the presence of defects in the
lattice such as, vacancies and pre-existing photoproducts. We also observe the
formation of Bjerrum defects following UV absorption and suggest that, together
with hydroxide anions, they are likely responsible for prominent features
experimentally detected in long UV exposure absorption spectra, remarkably
red-shifted relative to short exposure spectra. Our results highlight the key
role of defects in determining the onset of absorption and emission processes
in ice.

### [187] [Accelerating Correlated Wave Function Calculations with Hierarchical Matrix Compression of the Two-Electron Integrals](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.16576)
*Hongji Gao,Xiangmin Jiao,Benjamin G. Levine*

Main category: physics.chem-ph

TL;DR: 这是一个研究论文摘要，主要介绍了一种基于矩阵稀疏性的量子化学计算加速方法，提出了一种分层的 SOS-MP2 算法，通过将电子排斥积分张量采用矩阵 H² 格结构压缩，从而将计算时间和空间复杂度从 O(N²) 降低至 O(N² log N)，并展示了在多方面的测试中的渐近复杂度优势。


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: 矩阵稀疏性的利用在科学计算中非常重要，特别是在处理大规模的数据时，减少计算复杂度可以显著提高效率。量子化学中的电子排斥积分计算通常是高计算量的，引入 H² 格结构压缩是一种有效的优化方法。

Method: 该研究提出了适用于 MP2 计算的分层 SOS-MP2 算法，通过在电子排斥积分张量上应用 H² 格结构压缩，结合原子轨道的拉普拉斯变换，最大限度地利用数据稀疏性和能重密度矩阵的元素稀疏性。

Result: 该算法的成功应用使得 Coulomb-like 项的计算在 MP2 能量中以 O(N² log N) 的时间复杂度和空间复杂度进行，显著优于传统的 O(N²) 复杂度。数值测试显示这种加速策略在多方面的应用中都表现出了更好的渐近复杂度。

Conclusion: 这项研究展示了如何通过矩阵稀疏性和分层压缩技术，进一步优化了量子化学中的 MP2 方法计算。提出的方法在处理大分子和三维水分子时，计算复杂度得到了显著的提升， opens up 了更广泛的应用前景。

Abstract: Leveraging matrix sparsity has proven a fruitful strategy for accelerating
quantum chemical calculations. Here we present the hierarchical SOS-MP2
algorithm, which uses hierarchical matrix ($\mathcal{H}^{2}$) compression of
the electron repulsion integral (ERI) tensor to reduce both time and space
complexity. This approach is based on the atomic orbital Laplace transform MP2
calculations, leveraging the data sparsity of the ERI tensor and the
element-wise sparsity of the energy-weighted density matrices. The
$\mathcal{H}^{2}$ representation approximates the ERI tensor in a block
low-rank form, taking advantage of the inherent low-rank nature of the
repulsion integrals between distant sets of atoms. The resulting algorithm
enables the calculation of the Coulomb-like term of the MP2 energy with a
theoretical time complexity of $\mathcal{O}(N^{2}\log N)$ and a space
complexity of $\mathcal{O}(N^{2}\log N)$, where $N$ denotes the number of basis
functions. Numerical tests show asymptotic time and space complexities better
than $\mathcal{O}(N^{2})$ for both linear alkanes and three-dimensional water
clusters.

</details>


### [188] [Aufbau suppressed coupled cluster as a post-linear-response method](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.16680)
*Trine Kay Quady,Harrison Tuckman,Eric Neuscamman*

Main category: physics.chem-ph

TL;DR: Aufbau-suppressed coupled cluster can effectively improve the accuracy of linear response methods for electronically excited states, especially in charge transfer states, significantly reducing errors from starting points with multi-eV errors to 0.1 eV.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: The paper explores the application of a specific quantum method (Aufbau-suppressed coupled cluster) to enhance the accuracy of existing linear response methods, particularly for charge transfer states, which are known to be challenging.

Method: The method involves using the Aufbau-suppressed coupled cluster as a post-linear-response correction to improve the results of linear response methods.

Result: The study demonstrates that the Aufbau-suppressed coupled cluster method can significantly improve the accuracy of results, especially when used with less accurate starting points, converting errors of several eV into errors of about 0.1 eV.

Conclusion: The Aufbau-suppressed coupled cluster method shows promise as a viable alternative for initializing linear response methods, potentially offering accuracy comparable to more expensive methods.

Abstract: We investigate the ability of Aufbau suppressed coupled cluster theory to act
as a post-linear-response correction to widely used linear response methods for
electronically excited states. We find that the theory is highly resilient to
shortcomings in the underlying linear response method, with final results from
less accurate starting points nearly as good as those from the best starting
points. This pattern is especially stark in charge transfer states, where the
approach converts starting points with multi-eV errors into
post-linear-response results with errors on the order of 0.1 eV. These findings
highlight the ability of Aufbau suppressed coupled cluster to perform its own
orbital relaxations and raise the question of whether initializing it with an
orbital relaxed reference is worth the trouble.

Method: The authors developed a reduced-cost method using a SS-FNO framework, which includes systematic truncation of virtual spaces controlled by two adjustable thresholds. Abstract: We present a reduced-cost equation-of-motion coupled-cluster method for
excited states, built on a new state-specific frozen natural orbital (SS-FNO)
framework. This approach enables systematic and controllable truncation of the
virtual spaces, significantly reducing computational demands while maintaining
high accuracy. The method allows black-box application via two adjustable
thresholds and includes a perturbative correction that compensates for
truncation errors. We have tested the performance of both CIS(D) and ADC(2)
methods in generating appropriate natural orbitals for excited states.
Benchmarking on valence, Rydberg, and charge-transfer excited states
demonstrates excellent agreement with canonical EE-EOM-CCSD results, with mean
absolute deviations typically below 0.02 eV when ADC(2) natural orbitals with
perturbative corrections are applied.

### [191] [Coupled cluster method tailored by quantum selected configuration interaction](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.16911)
*Luca Erhart,Yuichiro Yoshida,Wataru Mizukami*

Main category: physics.chem-ph

TL;DR: The paper introduces the QSCI-TCC method, combining quantum and classical computing for efficient electronic structure calculations, demonstrated to handle systems that traditional methods struggle with.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Developing efficient quantum algorithms for chemical calculations, especially for systems too large for classical methods, seems important. The rise in quantum computing hardware with trapped ions and qubits, along with software like Cirq, Qiskit, and QubiC, supports this motivation.

Method: The QSCI-TCC method uses a quantum-selected CI wave function (QSCI) to reconstruct the many-electron state, then combines it with coupled-cluster (CC) theory in a tailored way. QSCI is implemented on a quantum computer using fewer qubits than traditional methods, and the CC framework optimizes the remaining amplitudes classically.

Result: QSCI-TCC provides accurate results for O-H bond dissociation in H2O and N2 triple-bond dissociation, outperforming CCSD and CCSD(T). Shot-count tests show fewer than 10^5 shots on a 6-electron/6-orbital active space achieve chemical accuracy, improving on earlier methods.

Conclusion: QSCI-TCC is a promising hybrid quantum-classical method for quantum-chemical calculations, using fewer resources than existing approaches while maintaining accuracy and handling strongly correlated systems efficiently.

Abstract: We present the quantum-selected configuration interaction-tailored
coupled-cluster (QSCI-TCC) method, a hybrid quantum-classical scheme that
tailors coupled-cluster (CC) theory with a quantum-selected configuration
interaction (QSCI) wave function. QSCI provides a scalable, shot-efficient
approach to reconstructing the many-electron state prepared on quantum hardware
on a classical computer. The resulting active-space CI coefficients, which are
free from additive shot noise, are mapped to fixed cluster amplitudes within
the tailored coupled-cluster framework, after which a conventional CC
calculation optimizes the remaining amplitudes. This workflow embeds static
(strong) correlation from the quantum device and subsequently recovers
dynamical (weak) correlation, yielding a balanced description of both. The
method is classically simulated and applied to the simultaneous O-H bond
dissociation in H$_2$O and the triple-bond dissociation in N$_2$. QSCI-TCC and
its perturbative-triples variant, QSCI-TCC(T), provide accurate results even
where CCSD or CCSD(T) begin to break down. Shot-count tests for the N$_2$ (6e,
6o) active space demonstrate that, with the (c) correction, chemically
sufficient precision ($\leq 1$ kcal/mol) is achieved with only $1.0 \times
10^5$ shots in the strongly correlated regime ($r=2.2$ \r{A}) -- an order of
magnitude fewer than required by an earlier matchgate-shadows implementation
[J. Chem. Theory Comput., 20, 5068 (2024)]. By pairing resource-efficient
quantum sampling with the CC theory, QSCI-TCC provides a promising pathway to
quantum-chemical calculations of classically intractable systems.

</details>

### [192] [Generalized Petermann factor of non-Hermitian systems at exceptional points](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.15807)
*Julius Kullig,Jan Wiersig,Henning Schomerus*

Main category: physics.optics

TL;DR: Error


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Error

Method: Error

Result: Error

Conclusion: Error

Abstract: The nonorthogonality of modes in open systems significantly modifies their
resonant response, resulting in quantitative and qualitative deviations from
Breit-Wigner resonance relations. For isolated resonances with a Lorentzian
lineshape, the deviations amount to an enhancement of the resonance linewidth
by the Petermann factor (PF), given by the overlap of left and right eigenmodes
of the underlying effectively non-Hermitian Hamiltonian. The PF diverges at
exceptional points (EPs), where resonance frequencies degenerate, and right and
left eigenmodes are orthogonal to each other. This divergence signifies a
qualitative departure from a Lorentzian lineshape, which has gained recent
attention. In this work, we extend this concept to EPs, and describe how this
EP PF manifests in a variety of physical scenarios. Firstly, we identify this
PF in physical terms as an enhancement of the response of a system to external
or parametric perturbations. Utilizing two natural orthogonally projected
reference systems based on the right and left eigenvectors, we show that each
choice carries a precise geometric interpretation that naturally extends the
notion of the PF for isolated resonances to EPs. The two choices can be
combined into an overall EP PF, which again can be expressed in purely
geometric terms. Secondly, we illuminate the geometric mechanisms that
determine the size of the EP PF, by considering the role of modes participating
in the degeneracy and those that remain spectrally separated. Thirdly, we
design a system to study the EP PF in a specific physical setup, consisting of
two microrings coupled to a waveguide with embedded semitransparent mirrors.
This example shows our approach yields a more accurate spectral response
strength than conventional truncation. These results complete the description
of systems at EPs in the same way as the original PF does for isolated
resonances.

</details>


### [193] [Slow Light Augmented Fabry-Perot Cavity for Enhanced Sensitivity in Measuring Frequency Shift](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.15885)
*Ruoxi Zhu,Zifan Zhou,Dustin Greenwood,Jason Bonacum,David D. Smith,Selim M. Shahriar*

Main category: physics.optics

TL;DR: 优化的法拉第-珀尔 cavity 能够显著提高激光频率测量灵敏度。


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: 提升激光频率测量灵敏度对于科学研究和应用非常关键。通过改进结构设计可以带来更好的性能。

Method: 通过引入慢光效应和 Fabry-Perot 柜架结构的设计，增强了灵敏度，针对两种不同的结构进行了详细分析和比较。

Result: 使用法拉第-珀尔 柜增加了约1.4万倍的灵敏度，性能优异。

Conclusion: 建议在实验中采用冷原子实现慢光效应，以优化设计达到更高的灵敏度水平。

Abstract: Recently, it has been shown that a slow-light augmented unbalanced
Mach-Zehnder interferometer (SLAUMZI) can be used to enhance significantly the
sensitivity of measuring the frequency shift of a laser, compared to the
conventional technique of heterodyning with a reference laser. Here, we show
that a similar enhancement can be realized using a slow-light augmented
Fabry-Perot Cavity (SLAFPC), due to the fact that an FPC is inherently
unbalanced, since different bounces of the field traverse different path
lengths before interfering with the other bounces. We show how the degree of
enhancement in sensitivity depends on the spectral width of the laser and the
finesse of the FPC. We also show how the sensitivity enhancement factor (SEF)
for the SLAFPC is much larger than the same for the SLAUMZI for comparable
conditions and the same group index, under lossless conditions. In general, the
effect of the loss caused by the medium that produces the slow-light process is
more prominent for the SLAFPC than the SLAUMZI. However, if the attenuation per
pass can be kept low enough while producing a high group index, using cold
atoms for generating the slow-light effect, for example, then the SEF for the
SLAFPC can be much higher than that for the SLAUMZI. For potentially realizable
conditions, we show that an SEF of ~1.4*10^5 can be achieved using a SLAFPC.

</details>

### [196] [Optical centrifuge for nanoparticles](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.16134)
*Peiyao Xiong,Kit Ka Kelvin Ho,J. M. H. Gosling,M. Rademacher,P. F. Barker*

<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: The study aimed to create precise control over rotation in nanoscale objects, which is fundamental for various applications in nanotechnology.

Method: They used optical tweezers and manipulated polarization to induce rotation, with numerical simulations to confirm stability.

Result: Nanorotors achieved over 100 MHz rotation within 100 microseconds.

Conclusion: This method offers a promising approach for precise control in micro/nanoscale systems, opening doors for future applications. Also, tools for polarization control were developed to facilitate this process.

Abstract: We study the creation of an optical centrifuge for the controlled rotation of
levitated nanorotors within an optical tweezer. The optical centrifuge is
created by rapidly rotating the linear polarization of the tightly focused
optical field used to form an optical trap. We show that nanorotors, formed by
anisotropic nanoparticles levitated within the trap, can be accelerated to
well-defined rotational rates in excess of 100 MHz over durations of hundreds
of microseconds. The initial conditions required for stable acceleration, based
on optical trap properties and the anisotropic susceptibility of the nanorotor
are established, and confirmed by numerical simulations. We also present
initial experiments that have developed tools for the rapid angular
acceleration of the polarization vector of the linearly polarized beam that is
required to create the centrifuge. We show that over the acceleration durations
in the 100 $\upmu$s range, high rotational speeds could be achieved in modest
vacuum.

Conclusion: 结论为超晶格材料的设计提供了参考，未来实验中将进一步优化载荷浓度和结构参数以提高光吸收性能。

Abstract: The plasmonic optical absorption of the silica glasses containing copper
selenide nanoparticles is simulated on the basis of Drude theory. The plasmonic

factor and the matrix dielectric function. The charge carrier concentration in
the nanoparticles is evaluated through the plasmonic frequency for the spectra
of closest correspondence to experimental. The plasmon resonance position and

Abstract: Polar solitons, i.e., solitonic waves accompanying asymmetry of geometry or
phase, have garnered attention in polar systems, such as ferroelectric or
magnetoelectric materials, where they play a critical role in topological
transitions and nonreciprocal responses to external fields. A key question is
whether such polar solitons can emerge in nonpolar systems, where intrinsic
polarity is absent. Here, we demonstrate an unprecedented polar soliton with

alternating electric field. The soliton is corn-kernel-shaped, displaying a

can be activated by controlling the voltage and frequency of an electric field.

balancing the electric and nematic elastic energies, while the flexoelectric
effect drives their rotational behaviors. The discovery of polar solitons in
nonpolar systems expands the understanding of topological solitons, opening new
avenues for dynamic control in soft matter systems, with potential applications
in nonreciprocal responsive materials and topological information storage.

### [203] [A Hybrid Zernike-Lyapunov Framework for Aberration-Based Statistical Wavefront Reconstruction of Chaotic Optical Surfaces](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.16847)
*Netzer Moriya*

Main category: physics.optics

<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: 随着光学系统复杂性的增加，混沌现象在光学系统中的应用越来越广泛，像光轴向扰动、光波传播等都与光轴向扰动理论密切相关，需要一种统一的方法来分析和解决。

Method: 通过将光线轨迹的偏转与波光相位扰动通过eikonal方程联系，将混沌波前扰动分解为修正的Zernike-Lyapunov混合展开，建立Lyapunov指数、分数维数和传统指数之间的数学等价关系，从而将非积分光轴向扰动纳入确定性设计框架，为有控制的光系统设计提供了理论基础。

Result: 论文通过相空间分析验证了框架的有效性，并确定了混沌展开的收敛标准。利用这一理论发现可以有意设计具有混沌表面几何的光学系统，实现如光束均匀化、斑点减少以及新的波前形成功能，同时保持了与传统扰动分析一样严谨的数学基础。

Conclusion: 论文为潜在应用创造了严格的数学基础，为基于可控的光谱设计提供了可靠的理论支撑。这项研究展示了如何通过系统性方法，利用混沌表面来实现预期的光学性能，拓展了光轴向扰动理论的实用领域。

Abstract: We present a comprehensive theoretical framework that unifies chaotic
wavefront dynamics with classical aberration theory through a Statistical
Wavefront Reconstruction Framework (SWRF) formalism. By establishing rigorous
connections between ray trajectory deflections and wave-optical phase
perturbations through the eikonal equation, we decompose chaotic wavefront
perturbations into modified Zernike-Lyapunov hybrid expansions, establishing
mathematical equivalences between Lyapunov exponents, fractal dimensions, and
traditional aberration coefficients. This chaotic aberration theory enables
systematic incorporation of non-integrable wavefront dynamics into
deterministic design frameworks, providing a rigorous foundation for controlled
chaos in optical systems. We derive analytical relationships connecting surface
chaos parameters to optical performance metrics, demonstrate the framework's
validity through phase space analysis, and establish convergence criteria for
the chaotic expansion. The theory reveals how chaotic surface geometries can be
intentionally designed to achieve specific optical functionalities, including
beam homogenization, speckle reduction, and novel wavefront shaping
capabilities, while maintaining mathematical rigor comparable to classical
aberration analysis.

  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: The paper addresses the challenge of efficiently shaping nonlinear light, which is crucial for various applications, and proposes a method using pump beam manipulation for better control.

Method: They investigate nonlinear spin-orbit conversion and use geometric phase through liquid crystal flat optical elements to generate vectorial modes in the second harmonic. Spatial wavefunctions and their propagation are also analyzed.

Result: They successfully demonstrate mode generation with invariance and effective spin-orbit conversion, opening new possibilities in harmonic systems.

Conclusion: This method offers an efficient approach to structuring nonlinear light, applicable in laser micromachining and high-energy physics. The success suggests broader applications in these fields with structured light sources.

Abstract: Nonlinear optics is crucial for shaping the spatial structure of shortwave
light and its interactions with matter, but achieving this through simple
harmonic generation with a single pump is challenging. This study demonstrates
nonlinear spin-orbit conversion using spin-dependent pump shaping via geometric
phase, allowing the direct creation of desired structured harmonic waves from a
Gaussian pump beam. By using the liquid-crystal flat optical elements
fabricated with photoalignment, we experimentally produce higher-order
cylindrically vectorial modes in second harmonic fields. We examine the
vectorial spatial wavefunctions, their propagation invariance, and nonlinear
spin-orbit conversion. Our results provide an efficient method for full
structuring nonlinear light in broader harmonic systems, with significant
applications in laser micromachining and high-energy physics.

Method: The study involves setting up a neutron detector and a polarimeter at the SAMURAI terminal. gives rise to the nuclear symmetry energy. The simulations studies on the
experimental measurement of IVR effect using SAMURAI terminal at RIKEN Nishina
center have been performed to demonstrate the feasibility of the experiment. By
introducing a well designed polarimeter to detect the
$\mathrm{p}(\vec{\mathrm{d}}, \mathrm{d})\mathrm{p}$ elastic scattering, the
monitoring of the tensor polarization of deuteron beam can be implemented. The
protons and neutrons produced by the breakup of polarized deuterons scattering
off heavy targets are designed to be measured by proton drift chamber (PDC)
combined with the SAMURAI magnet and NEBULA detector, respectively. The
detector responses are simulated using Geant4 framework, while the events of
the deuteron elastic breakup are generated by an Improved Quantum Molecular

demonstrate the feasibility to detect the IVR effect at SAMURAI with both

<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>

Method: 使用了64x64的pgSPADs阵列，通过调整栅门电压以利用设备的固有暗计数率，再使用Classical Von Neumann算法进行去偏。

Abstract: Random number generators that utilize arrays of entropy source elements
suffer from bias variation (BV). Despite the availability of efficient
debiasing algorithms, optimized implementations of hardware friendly options
depend on the bit bias in the raw bit streams and cannot accommodate a wide BV.
In this work, we present a 64 x 64 array of perimeter gated single photon
avalanche diodes (pgSPADs), fabricated in a 0.35 {\mu}m standard CMOS
technology, as a source of entropy to generate random binary strings with a BV
compensation technique. By applying proper gate voltages based on the devices'
native dark count rates, we demonstrate less than 1% BV for a raw-bit
generation rate of 2 kHz/pixel at room temperature. The raw bits were debiased
using the classical iterative Von Neumann's algorithm and the debiased bits
were found to pass all of the 16 tests from NIST's Statistical Test Suite.

This paper contributes to that field by presenting new measurements and confirming the detectors' viability for the required specifications.

are required in a single photon mode. Quantum Efficiency (QE) has been measured
for the first batch of EIC HRPPDs both by Incom and EIC research groups at
Jefferson Lab and Brookhaven Lab, with peak values at $\sim$365 nm typically
exceeding 30%. In this study, we present a first direct measurement of HRPPD
Photon Detection Efficiency (PDE) being equal to 19.3 $\pm$ 0.2 (stat) $\pm$
0.8 (sys)% at 398.6 nm, in a photoelectron pulse counting mode using a
picosecond diode laser. HRPPD QE at the same spot and at the same wavelength
was evaluated to be 24.3 $\pm$ 0.1 (stat) $\pm$ 0.5 (sys)%, leading to a
Collection Efficiency (CE) estimate of $\sim$79%, which is consistent with the
expectations.

### [217] [Improvement of Nuclide Detection through Graph Spectroscopic Analysis Framework and its Application to Nuclear Facility Upset Detection](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.16522)

Abstract: We present a method to improve the detection limit for radionuclides using
spectroscopic radiation detectors and the arrival time of each detected
radiation quantum. We enable this method using a neural network with an
attention mechanism. We illustrate the method on the detection of Cesium
release from a nuclear facility during an upset, and our method shows $2\times$
improvement over the traditional spectroscopic method. We hypothesize that our
method achieves this performance increase by modulating its detection
probability by the overall rate of probable detections, specifically by
adapting detection thresholds based on temporal event distributions and local
spectral features, and show evidence to this effect. We believe this method is
applicable broadly and may be more successful for radionuclides with more
complicated decay chains than Cesium; we also note that our method can
generalize beyond the addition of arrival time and could integrate other data
about each detection event, such as pulse quality, location in detector, or
even combining the energy and time from detections in different detectors.

### [220] [Ultracold collisions of a neutral atom with a trapped ion in 1D](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.15804)
*Seth T. Rittenhouse,Lorenzo Oghittu,Arghavan Safavi-Naini,Rene Gerritsma,Nirav P. Mehta*

Main category: physics.atom-ph

TL;DR: 文章详细分析了^6Li原子和^171Yb+离子在1维空间中的量子散射，通过极坐标重新表述和adiabatic表示法提取出多种 Wentzel-Kramers-Brillouin (WKB)势能面，利用量子缺陷理论方法引入了一个相位参数来描述短程相互作用。研究发现，在低碰撞能量下，散射截面出现了规则排列的共振峰，这与量子混沌和BGS猜想的预期不符。


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: 研究量子系统中散射共振的结构和分布，特别是在不同离子间的相互作用中，这有助于理解原子和离子的捕获和散射机制，同时可能与量子混沌理论相悖。

Method: 详细研究了一维自由^6Li原子与被捕捉的^171Yb+离子之间的散射，使用极坐标重新表述和adiabatic表示法，提取多势能面，引入相位参数描述短程行为，研究低能量下的共振模式。

Result: 在低碰撞能量下观察到规则排列的共振峰，与量子混沌与BGS猜想预期有悖。

Conclusion: 提出在不同 trap 状态下的量子势能面及其对原子离子散射的影响，指出低能量下的规则共振模式可能提供新的研究视角。

Abstract: We present a fully quantum mechanical description of a free $^6$Li atom
scattering from a trapped $^{171}$Yb$^+$ ion in one dimension. By reformulating
the system in polar coordinates and employing the adiabatic representation, we
extract a set of coupled adiabatic potentials representing the atom interacting
with the ion in different trap states. In an approach similar to quantum defect
theory (QDT), we leverage the vast difference in energy scale between the
interaction, the trap, and the scattering energy to encapsulate the short-range
atom-ion scattering behavior in a single phase parameter. The presence of
trapped $({}^{171}\text{Yb}^6\text{Li})^+$ molecular-ion states leads to a
series of roughly evenly spaced resonances in the scattering cross section. The
predicted distribution of resonances at low collision energies is at odds with
the expectation of quantum chaos and the Bohigas-Giannoni-Schmit (BGS)
conjecture.

### [221] [Short-Range Hard-Sphere Potential and Coulomb Interaction: Deser-Trueman Formula for Rydberg States of Exotic Atomic Systems](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.15973)
*G. S. Adkins,U. D. Jentschura*

Main category: physics.atom-ph

TL;DR: 该论文提出了一种广义的Deser-Trueman公式，用于计算带状氢原子能级在强相互作用下的能量校正。主量子数n和角量子数l的组合决定了这种能量校正，其中高阶l值导致效果被显著压制。数值模拟证实了公式的准确性。


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: 该研究旨在解决在复杂原子系统中难以估计强相互作用下能量修正的问题，尤其是在寻找新物理方面，这可能是一个关键突破。

Method: 论文使用了推导式分析法，首先得出一般性的能量修正公式，并通过在指数点阵上的20,000点数值模拟进行了验证。

Result: 研究得出能量修正与主量子数n和角量子数l相关，公式中高l值显著降低修正效果，数值结果与推导结果一致。

Conclusion: 该工作提供了一种有效的方法来估算强相互作用对原子能级的影响，对于寻找低能新物理具有潜在的应用价值。

Abstract: In exotic atomic systems with hadronic constituent particles, it is
notoriously difficult to estimate the strong-interaction correction to energy
levels. It is well known that, due to the strength of the nuclear interaction,
the problem cannot be treated on the basis of Wigner-Brioullin perturbation
theory. Recently, high-angular-momentum Rydberg states of exotic atomic systems
with hadronic constituents have been identified as promising candidates for the
search of New Physics in the low-energy sector of the Standard Model. In order
to render this endeavor feasible, it is necessary to estimate the
strong-interaction correction to the atomic energy levels. We thus derive a
generalized Deser-Trueman formula for the induced energy shift for a general
hydrogenic bound state with principal quantum number $n$ and orbital angular
momentum quantum number~$\ell$, and find that the energy shift is given by the
formula delta E = 2 alpha_{n, L} beta_L (a_h/a_0)^(2 L + 1) E_h/n^3, where
alpha_{n,0} = 1, alpha_{n,L} is the product from s=1 to s=L of the expression
(s^(-2) - n^(-2)), beta_L = (2 L + 1)/[(2 L + 1)!!]^2, where E_h is the Hartree
energy, a_h is the hadronic radius and a_0 is the generalized Bohr radius. The
square of the double factorial, [(2\ell + 1)!!]^2, in the denominator implies a
somewhat fortunate, drastic suppression of the effect for higher angular
momenta. The results are verified by numerical calculations on an exponential
lattice with 20,000 points.

</details>


### [222] [Detection of twisted radiowaves with Rydberg atoms](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.16368)
*P. O. Kazinski,P. S. Korolev,V. A. Ryakin*

TL;DR: Error

  <summary>Details</summary>

Abstract: The dynamics of the outer electron in an alkali atom in the presence of
structured electromagnetic waves is described. The interaction of the alkali
Rydberg atom with twisted radiowaves is considered. The two schemes for
Rydberg-atom based detector of twisted radiowaves are proposed. According to
the theoretical model for these detectors, they can record a source of twisted
radiowaves with power down to several nW. The first scheme of the detector
employs the nondipole transitions between Rydberg states induced by twisted
radio photons. The second scheme involves the array of Rydberg-atom based
antennas, every antenna measuring the dipole transitions excited by plane
radiowaves comprising the twisted one.

### [223] [CaF+CaF interactions in the ground and excited electronic states: implications for collisional losses](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.16897)
*Dibyendu Sardar,Marcin Gronowski,Michał Tomza,John L. Bohn*

Main category: physics.atom-ph

TL;DR: 研究通过计算基态和激发态的势能曲面，揭示了激光冷却CaF分子在碰撞过程中非反应性、自旋极化表面的损失机制。


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: 准确计算基本态和激发态的势能曲面对于理解超冷分子碰撞结果至关重要。研究利用多参考自洽单双激发法和较大量子空间，计算了Ca2F2在刚性转子近似下的12个电子态。同时计算了自旋轨道耦合和自旋自旋耦合，并确定了几种电容跃迁偶极矩，发现最低自旋极化态与多个激发态相交，解释了碰撞损失的可能途径。

Method: 使用多参考自洽单双激发方法和较大自旋空间，计算了12个电子态，计算了自旋轨道和自旋自旋耦合，以及电容跃迁偶极矩。

Result: 发现最低自旋极化态与多个激发态重叠，结合势能曲面分析，合理解释了非反应性自旋极化表面的碰撞损失机制。

Conclusion: 研究为理解超冷CaF分子碰撞中的自旋极化损失提供了理论基础。通过分析势能曲面，指出了可能的碰撞机制。这为未来优化冷却技术提供参考。

Abstract: Accurate \textit{ab initio} potential energy surfaces are essential to
understand and predict collisional outcomes in ultracold molecular systems. In
this study, we explore the intermolecular interactions between two laser-cooled
CaF molecules, both in their ground and excited electronic states, aiming to
understand the mechanisms behind the observed collisional losses on the
non-reactive, spin-polarized surface of the CaF+CaF system. Using
state-of-the-art \textit{ab initio} methods, we compute twelve electronic
states of the Ca$_2$F$_2$ complex within the rigid rotor approximation applied
to CaF. Calculating the potential energy surfaces for the excited electronic
states of Ca$_2$F$_2$ is challenging and computationally expensive. Our
approach employs the multireference configuration interaction method,
restricted to single and double excitations, along with a reasonably large
active space to ensure the convergence in the excited states. We also compute
the spin-orbit coupling between the ground state and the lowest spin-polarized
triplet state, as well as the spin-spin coupling within the lowest triplet
state (1) $^3\mathrm{A}'$. Additionally, we determine the electric transition
dipole moments for the (1) $^3\mathrm{A}'$-(2) $^3\mathrm{A}'$ and (1)
$^3\mathrm{A}'$-(1) $^3\mathrm{A}''$ transitions. Notably, we find that the
lowest spin-polarized state (1) $^3\mathrm{A}'$, shifted by 1064 nm of laser
light from the optical dipole trap, intersects several electronically excited
states. Finally, by analyzing the potential energy surfaces, we discuss two
plausible pathways that may account for the observed collisional losses on the
spin-polarized surface of the CaF+CaF system.

</details>

### [224] [Theory of wakefield in a transversely inhomogeneous plasma waveguide](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.16200)
*K. V. Galaydych,P. I. Markov,G. V. Sotnikov*

Main category: physics.acc-ph

TL;DR: This paper discusses the generation of relativistic drive bunches in a cylindrical plasma wakefield. It models a transversely inhomogeneous plasma as a combination of tubular plasma and a dense plasma background. Analytical expressions for electric and magnetic fields are derived, along with dispersion and field topography investigations. The paper also provides structures of amplitude distributions and spectrum analysis of the wakefields, revealing their frequency content.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: The work is relevant to understanding plasma wakefield acceleration, a method for generating high-energy particles used in laser-molecule interactions and particle physics applications.

Method: Theoretical approach, modeling plasma as a combination of fluids with different densities. Derived analytical expressions for field components. Investigated dispersion and field topography. Performed spectrum analysis on wakefield components to determine their frequency content.

Result: Theoretical findings include derived field expressions, field topography, and frequency characteristics of wakefields, showing how the plasma structure affects bunch generation.

Conclusion: The research aids in designing plasma structures for efficient wakefield acceleration, which is crucial for particle and laser physics applications.

Abstract: Theoretical studies have been made into the relativistic drive bunch
generation of a wakefield in a cylindrical waveguide filled with a transversely
inhomogeneous plasma. According to the model used, the transversely
inhomogeneous plasma is considered as a combination of tubular plasma and the
plasma background of different density. Analytical expressions have been
derived for the excited radial and axial electric field components, and for the
azimuthal magnetic field component. The dispersion of the plasma waveguide
under study, as well as the topography of the electromagnetic field components
of the TM-eigenwaves, resonant with the bunch, have been investigated.
Longitudinal and transverse amplitude distribution structures of the axial and
radial wakefields have been determined. Spectrum analysis of the longitudinal
and transverse wakefields has been performed with the result that their
frequency content has been determined.

The authors propose avoiding conversion past an optimum wavelength to maximize power output and improve efficiency.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: The paper addresses a critical issue in space applications for photovoltaic devices: excessive heat generation caused by infrared tail conversion. High operating temperatures can reduce device efficiency and lifespan, making it necessary to find an optimal solution.

Method: The authors formulate a objective function involving energy conversion, heat generation, and efficiency to determine the optimal cutoff wavelength. They derive an analytical solution that considers the relationship between wavelength and device performance, leading to an optimal operating condition.

Result: By avoiding conversion past the optimum wavelength, the photovoltaic devices can achieve higher electrical power output and better heat distribution, thus maximizing efficiency and prolonging performance before end-of-life.

Conclusion: The paper suggests that limiting infrared tail conversion to an optimal point can mitigate excessive heat and improve the overall performance and longevity of space-based photovoltaic systems.

Abstract: Space applications require the highest performing photovoltaic devices.
Typically these are multi-junction devices that are capable of converting a
larger bandwidth of the solar spectrum. However, the conversion of longer
wavelength photons in the solar infrared tail results in a disproportionate
increase in generated heat per watt of electricity, and since devices have
limited heat rejection in space, this excess heat raises the operating
temperature, lowering the efficiency of the entire device. Here we show that
space-based photovoltaics should avoid converting the solar infrared tail past
an optimum terminal cutoff wavelength, and that this will lead to higher
electrical output. In addition, a lower operating temperature may lead to
higher end-of-life power outputs.

Abstract: This paper investigates the dynamics of nonholonomic mechanical systems, with

the transpositional rule. We analyze how the $\check Cetaev condition and the

### [233] [On the action for a charged particle moving in a magnetic field](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.16181)
*Manoj K. Harbola*

Main category: physics.class-ph

TL;DR: The paper presents an alternative method to determine the canonical momentum and quantize a charged particle in a magnetic field using the Maupertuis principle.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: The paper addresses the need for a different approach to apply Bohr-Wilson-Sommerfeld quantization without relying on Lagrangian mechanics.

Method: The authors use the Maupertuis principle of least action to derive canonical momentum and quantize a charged particle in a uniform magnetic field by incorporating flux through the trajectory.

Result: The method successfully utilizes action principles and flux to achieve quantization without needing the vector potential or Lagrangian approaches.

Conclusion: This approach provides a simpler and more intuitive method for students and researchers by avoiding complex Lagrangian formulations.

Abstract: Application of the Bohr-Wilson-Sommerfeld quantization condition to a charged
particle in a uniform magnetic field requires knowledge of the canonical
momentum of such a particle, which in turn requires students to know about the
vector potential. The canonical momentum in this situation is conventionally
obtained by introducing an appropriate additional term involving the
corresponding vector potential in the Lagrangian. In this work, we take a
different approach to this problem by analyzing it with Maupertuis principle of
least action. We show that satisfying this principle for a charged particle
moving in a uniform magnetic field requires that a term proportional to the
flux passing through the area enclosed by the trajectory of the particle be
included in its action. This additional term accomplishes two tasks. First, it
facilitates applying the Bohr-Wilson-Sommerfeld quantum condition for a charged
particle moving in a uniform magnetic field without using the Lagrangian
approach, and, secondly, it gives the appropriate canonical momentum and
Lagrangian for a charged particle in a general electromagnetic field in a
straightforward manner.

</details>

Method: The authors use the Transfer Matrix Method to model plane wave propagation and its extensions to calculate sensitivity of modal parameters to geometric changes. They apply this in a soprano saxophone model to optimize octave harmonicity.

Result: They successfully demonstrate how geometric adjustments can predictively improve the instrument's performance, aiding both sound synthesis and design.

Conclusion: The analytical approach using sensitivity analysis offers a significant breakthrough for wind instrument tuning and design.

Abstract: The Transfer Matrix Method is a practical approach for modeling plane wave
propagation in one-dimensional waveguides. Its simplicity makes it especially
attractive for accounting for viscothermal losses, enabling realistic
simulations of complex waveguides such as wind instruments. Another strength of
this method lies in its fully analytical formulation of wave propagation. Modal
parameters naturally arise as by-products of the model, obtained by numerically
solving analytical expressions. In this work, the analytical potential of the
method is extended by deriving the sensitivity of modal parameters to changes
in the geometry of the resonator. These analytical gradients are applied in the
context of wind instrument design. A simplified model of a soprano saxophone is
used to investigate how octave harmonicity can be optimized through small
geometric adjustments. The proposed approach enables predictive adjustments of
geometry and offers valuable insight for both sound synthesis and instrument
making.

</details>
